  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8b2a0a53-3d92-420e-b9c3-4b48823679b6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText14406749849204099024" style="display:none"><b>When a TV reporter is injured in a Dallas-bound jet crash, she enters a world of mistaken identity and political intrigue in this action-packed romantic suspense novel -- a <i>Globe and Mail </i>bestseller!</b><b>
  <br />
</b> The crash of a Dallas-bound jet isn't just a tragedy for TV reporter Avery Daniels; it's an act of fate that hands her a golden opportunity to further her career. But it also makes her the crucial player in a drama of violent passions and deadly desires.<br /><br /> After plastic surgery transforms her face, Avery is mistaken for the glamorous, selfish wife of Tate Rutledge, the famous senatorial candidate and member of a powerful Texas dynasty.<br /><br /> As she lays helpless in the hospital, Avery makes a shattering discovery: someone close to Tate planned to assassinate him. Now, to save him, she must live another woman's life -- and risk her own.<br /><br /><br /></span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/61879040-lea-kane"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1495607140i/61879040._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/61879040-lea-kane">Lea Kane</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Excellent question, and I have no idea why. Also, earlier in the book Nelson &amp; Carole were at the table eating with no one else around, &amp; he didn't tr<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Excellent question, and I have no idea why. Also, earlier in the book Nelson &amp; Carole were at the table eating with no one else around, &amp; he didn't treat her as a co-conspirator. He was acting fatherly, glad she had changed for the better. Makes no sense if he brought her on board to make Tate miserable. There is also a remark in the end of the book by Avery claiming he was still a good father. I was like WTF?<br /><br />And why would they wait until after he won the election to do this? They could have shot him on stage at any point during the election in front of all the cameras etc.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1972933932?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1972933932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13358163084459714349"><b>5 stars for enjoyment minus 1 star for a very enjoyable but VERY unrealistic plot</b><br/><br/>I'd be lying if I said I didn't love this book. It’s one of my favorites by SB. I practically inhaled it. It's equally focused on the romance as it is on the suspense.<br/><br/>But let’s be real. The legs on which this story stands are loose and wobbly. The heroine undergoes a facial surgical reconstruction after she survives a plane crash. After the surgery, she looks exactly like another woman who died in the plane crash. <i>N</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13358163084459714349" style="display:none"><b>5 stars for enjoyment minus 1 star for a very enjoyable but VERY unrealistic plot</b><br><br>I'd be lying if I said I didn't love this book. It’s one of my favorites by SB. I practically inhaled it. It's equally focused on the romance as it is on the suspense.<br><br>But let’s be real. The legs on which this story stands are loose and wobbly. The heroine undergoes a facial surgical reconstruction after she survives a plane crash. After the surgery, she looks exactly like another woman who died in the plane crash. <i>Nobody</i> in her new family notices she is not who they think she is. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507573770ra/24128450.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I'm sorry but I'm not buying it. What about her body shape? Her legs, her arms, her hands, her nails, her butt, her speech, her accent, her mannerisms? What about her eyes? Granted, they had the same eye color, but come on… Your eyes <i>always</i> give you away. I’m not even sure if it’s possible today (and let alone twenty years ago) to reconstruct one’s face to look <i>exactly</i> as it did before it was completely smashed and burned. Let alone <i>somebody else's</i> face.<br><br>Anyhow, she’s got a new face and she gets used to it immediately. In two months she’s good as new. She even travels around by plane. After the <i>plane crash</i>. No psychological issues at all. She doesn’t need a therapist. She’s one of the 14 people that survived the crash. Everybody else DIED. Even her “daughter” has nightmares, for god’s sake. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507573770ra/24128450.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I’m not sure what to say about the heroine. I liked her in the beginning but I soon started to despise her. I didn’t agree with her choices and decisions. There were even moments when I wanted to slap some sense into her. With gusto.<br><br>I know what you think. How can I rate this book so highly if I have so many issues? Believe it or not, I managed to turn a blind eye. And the story <i>was</i> gripping thanks to the author's vivid imagination, great writing and excellent characterization. Tate (the hero) was HAWT. I love SB's heroes! And I enjoyed the suspense. I was biting my nails, <s>hoping</s>waiting for somebody to expose the heroine. Plus, I wasn’t sure who the bad guy was till the very end. <br><br>Though, come to think of it, I have a few questions. Feel free to answer them :)<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>1)	Why did the killer wait until after Tate won the election? <br>2)	Why did Eddie shoot Nelson? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>QUICK REVIEW:</b><br><br>Enjoyment: 5/5<br>Writing style: 5/5<br>Storyline: Unratable. It was extremely interesting and gripping but unrealistic. <br>Hero: 5/5<br>Heroine: 3/5<br>Secondary characters: 5/5 <br>Hotness/steam level: 3/5 <br>Romance: 4/5 <br>Angst level: 2.5/5<br>Darkness level: 1/5<br>Humor: 2/5<br>Depth of the book: 4/5<br>POV: multiple, third person<br>Triggers: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[plane crash, shooting, annyoing heroine <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510504825i/24426022._SX540_.jpg" width='400"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13358163084459714349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2216299774702973643">Mirror Image is another one to add to my favorites list of Sandra Brown books. I think Avery and Tate are one of my favorite couples.<br/><br/><a href='http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/two_zps00ea5fc7.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>As with all my other reviews for her books I’m not going to say too much about the plot because it is so much better to jump into her stories without too much floating around in your mind. The synopsis gives you all you really need to know.<br/><br/>I wasn’t sure how SB was going to pull off this plot thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText2216299774702973643" style="display:none">Mirror Image is another one to add to my favorites list of Sandra Brown books. I think Avery and Tate are one of my favorite couples.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/two_zps00ea5fc7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419803539i/13128822.jpg" alt=" photo two_zps00ea5fc7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This one takes us to beautiful Texas to the Rocking R Ranch. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/1c67acf5c35903525cb0f102947da0c9_zpsd52d2b73.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419803539i/13128823.jpg" alt=" photo 1c67acf5c35903525cb0f102947da0c9_zpsd52d2b73.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As with all my other reviews for her books I’m not going to say too much about the plot because it is so much better to jump into her stories without too much floating around in your mind. The synopsis gives you all you really need to know.<br><br>I wasn’t sure how SB was going to pull off this plot though. How can someone just take over another person’s life in every essence? Kept an open mind and it paid off!! <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/3ab20f459cc2292eb3ee6f0501599e8a_zps39707248.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Things that happened just moments before the crash had to be an act of fate. The one thing that could have clearly identified Avery was no longer with her.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/4b797c7f79b9770b585309e28053d09c_zps10260706.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419803539i/13128825.jpg" alt=" photo 4b797c7f79b9770b585309e28053d09c_zps10260706.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But Avery Daniels had her reasons for becoming Carol Rutledge. And there were a few times when she ached for things to be different. But then came the point when there was no turning back. Tate Rutledge was a man she wanted to protect, a man who stole her heart.<br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/09e64e92db84680e3ab36aecce1307b9_zps7c831a43.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419803540i/13128826.jpg" alt=" photo 09e64e92db84680e3ab36aecce1307b9_zps7c831a43.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Tate and Avery drove me crazy, in all the most wonderful ways possible! With the basis of how their relationship began there was no way things were going to end well right? Well, SB takes these two through some intense moments, some freaking sensual sexy moments and some moments that caused me a bit of anxiety. <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/fancyampirish_zps560cf120.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419803540i/13128827.jpg" alt=" photo fancyampirish_zps560cf120.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There were many suspects that kept me guessing right to the end. There were interesting side characters as usual. My two favorites are Fancy and Irish. They both added that extra something to the story that I love.<br><br>Definitely another highly recommended read from me!!<br><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7812519775117940261">4.5 Stars<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The crash of a Dallas-bound jet wasn't just a tragedy to TV reporter Avery Daniels; it was an act of fate that handed her a golden opportunity to further her career. Mistaken for a glamorous, selfish woman named Carole Rutledge, the badly injured Avery would find that plastic surgery had given her Carole's face, the famous senatorial candidate Tate Rutledge for a husband, and a powerful Texas dynasty for in-laws. And as she lay helpless in the hospital, she would make a shatteri</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText7812519775117940261" style="display:none">4.5 Stars<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The crash of a Dallas-bound jet wasn't just a tragedy to TV reporter Avery Daniels; it was an act of fate that handed her a golden opportunity to further her career. Mistaken for a glamorous, selfish woman named Carole Rutledge, the badly injured Avery would find that plastic surgery had given her Carole's face, the famous senatorial candidate Tate Rutledge for a husband, and a powerful Texas dynasty for in-laws. And as she lay helpless in the hospital, she would make a shattering discovery: Someone close to Tate planned to assassinate him. Now, to save Tate's life, Avery must live another woman's life and risk her own</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>OK, you sort of have to suspend the disbelief here a bit. Some of the story is a bit implausible but go with the flow and enjoy it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>There was a lot about the man to admire. From the crown of his tousled brown hair to the toes of his scuffed boots, he was a man's man and a woman's fantasy</b>

  <b>But for every ardent admirer, he had an equally ardent enemy</b>
</blockquote><br><br>There was politics, friendships, newsroom drama, families, jealousies!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416607652i/12016210._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>Something stunck in Camelot</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416607652i/12016211.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Again, I won't say too much. You are better off just diving in. Yes, I was second guessing most people. Was wrong, as usual. That is the beauty of the writing of Ms Brown, she can make everyone a suspect.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Sweet revenge sometimes required bitter sacrifices</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416607652i/12016212._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I don't have a choice."</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Sex scenes were smoking hot as usual.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416607652i/12016213._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>So why not 5 stars? Again, I think it is because I love the books where the main male character is a bit of an ass and he is the one under suspicion too. Tate was not under suspicion here.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416607652i/12016214._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene Sim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene Sim" href="/user/show/31914348-irene-sim">Irene Sim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9602460806" href="/book/show/22442333">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31914348-irene-sim?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31914348-irene-sim?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1930254935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10064837528486628922">Re-read 28/10/17. <br/>As I was dusting my shelves the other day, I just took it in my hands and... put it back the next day after I blew my currently reading books and re-read this instead. One might believe that if you read a mystery book once, then there's no point in re-reading it once the plot is unveiled. But the second time you pay attention to all the little clues that the author put for you to find but were unaware the first time. For me, it says a lot about how talented an author SB is. And</span>
  <span id="freeText10064837528486628922" style="display:none">Re-read 28/10/17. <br />As I was dusting my shelves the other day, I just took it in my hands and... put it back the next day after I blew my currently reading books and re-read this instead. One might believe that if you read a mystery book once, then there's no point in re-reading it once the plot is unveiled. But the second time you pay attention to all the little clues that the author put for you to find but were unaware the first time. For me, it says a lot about how talented an author SB is. And all the feelings that I experienced the first time were there as well. I loved it equally this second time and I'm sure there will be many re-reads in the future.<br /><br />This one became one of my favorite. I will certainly re-read again in the future. Sandra Brown knows how to write romantic suspense. I loved it....</span>
  <a data-text-id="10064837528486628922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_559561698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/559561698" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2453991-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548801525p2/2453991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/559561698?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/2453991-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559561698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16461987107177648634">The story line for this book could have been interesting but honestly, I couldn't stand any of the characters.<br/><br/>Tate Rutledge is running for senator when his wife Carole is involved in a horrific plane crash - she and his 3-year-old daughter are one of few survivors of the fiery crash. Although Tate has no love lost for Carole, he feels responsible for helping her since she's his wife, and he makes sure she gets the best plastic surgery money can buy to return her face to its former splendor. <br/><br/>The </span>
  <span id="freeText16461987107177648634" style="display:none">The story line for this book could have been interesting but honestly, I couldn't stand any of the characters.<br /><br />Tate Rutledge is running for senator when his wife Carole is involved in a horrific plane crash - she and his 3-year-old daughter are one of few survivors of the fiery crash. Although Tate has no love lost for Carole, he feels responsible for helping her since she's his wife, and he makes sure she gets the best plastic surgery money can buy to return her face to its former splendor. <br /><br />The only problem is, Carole died in the plane crash, and a reporter, Avery Daniels, who had switched seats with her during the flight, has been mistaken for Carole. Unable to communicate in any way, she undergoes surgery and comes out as Carole's spitting image. While recovering, Avery plans to tell Tate the truth as soon as she's able, but then it comes to her that she can boost her own reporting career if she remains as Carole Rutledge and reports on the campaign from the inside...and then, when a mysterious visitor clues her in that Carole was in cahoots with someone close to Tate to murder him before he took office, Avery decides she must keep the facade to save Tate's life. <br /><br />I disliked the book because I really disliked Avery. A woman stupid enough to try to save her career by pretending to be another person's wife and someone's mother, and then falling in love with them and that cementing their decision to do so is just plan dumb. She was risking both her own professional career and Tate's eventual love because she convinced herself that only if she were faking being Carole could she find out who was behind it all (and yeah, it didn't help her at all...turns out people who aren't involved at all figure it out way before her).<br /><br />The real Carole was a real piece of work who doesn't even seem realistic. The ending also doesn't seem plausible or realistic at all. I usually like Brown's books but for me this one was a real dud...and some of the sex scenes, the descriptions were laughable. Something about his semen coating her womb? Like...what?? Who says that??<br /><br />Definitely don't recommend this particular book, although I do think Brown is a talented writer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16461987107177648634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2674728166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2674728166" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3919132-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507125560p2/3919132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2674728166?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/3919132-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/6397602-mirror-image">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=blackmail-criminal-plot-or-murder">blackmail-criminal-plot-or-murder</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=suspension-of-disbelief">suspension-of-disbelief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=some-outdated-information">some-outdated-information</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=dysfunctional-family">dysfunctional-family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=mistaken-identity">mistaken-identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=1990s">1990s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2674728166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8325143316430830071"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/685788.Mirror_Image' title='Mirror Image by Sandra Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mirror Image</a> was an older romantic suspense story published in 1990. I originally put it on my to-read list because it was recommended on several blogs by readers with similar tastes as mine. I thought the story was entertaining. <br/><br/><b>But be aware</b>, this was a buddy-read and I was clearly in the minority with my rating. <i>We had 174 comments among the seven of us.</i> Most of us agreed the suspense was good in the beginning though the plot was OTT and the main characters were not always likable. Especially </span>
  <span id="freeText8325143316430830071" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/685788.Mirror_Image" title="Mirror Image by Sandra Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Mirror Image</a> was an older romantic suspense story published in 1990. I originally put it on my to-read list because it was recommended on several blogs by readers with similar tastes as mine. I thought the story was entertaining. <br /><br /><b>But be aware</b>, this was a buddy-read and I was clearly in the minority with my rating. <i>We had 174 comments among the seven of us.</i> Most of us agreed the suspense was good in the beginning though the plot was OTT and the main characters were not always likable. Especially Avery, the heroine. There were also a couple of gender-offensive remarks that I found surprising to see; I don’t ever recall finding this in other stories by Ms. Brown. And I agree as my GR friends, they were insulting and unnecessary. <br /><br />So why four stars? When I am continually kept guessing and the tension mounts, I like that. At one time or another I thought the villain could have been every member of the Rutledges including Eddy, Tate’s campaign manager. In hindsight, there were several clues as to the motive that I overlooked. The author maneuvered my thoughts with this dysfunctional family and the off-the-wall romance. <br /><br /><b>A big <u>thank you</u> to Lyuda, Luli, Nefise, Nadine, Georgie and Jill for all of your insight.</b> Here is hoping the next BR will be better for everyone. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8325143316430830071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_324460551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/324460551" />
    <a title="Jonetta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta"><img alt="Jonetta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329083158p2/4876540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/324460551?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonetta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonetta" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta">Jonetta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/13543626-mirror-image">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer324460551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11423492509362172650">Avery Daniels was in a plane crash and survived. However, she awoke and found herself badly injured with no way to communicate and was mistakenly identified as someone else. Everyone now believes she's Carole Rutledge, wife of the Texas U.S. senatorial candidate Tate Rutledge. While recuperating in the hospital from surgery to restore her face but before she regains the ability to communicate, someone lets her in on the plan to assassinate Tate but she doesn't know the identity of that person. A</span>
  <span id="freeText11423492509362172650" style="display:none">Avery Daniels was in a plane crash and survived. However, she awoke and found herself badly injured with no way to communicate and was mistakenly identified as someone else. Everyone now believes she's Carole Rutledge, wife of the Texas U.S. senatorial candidate Tate Rutledge. While recuperating in the hospital from surgery to restore her face but before she regains the ability to communicate, someone lets her in on the plan to assassinate Tate but she doesn't know the identity of that person. Avery makes the decision to continue to impersonate Carole and figure out the identity of the killer.<br /><br />As with most mystery/suspense stories, you cannot say too much about them without spoiling the experience for other readers. What I liked about this book was that it took a while for everything to unfold and I was learning about the other characters at the same time as Avery. The developing romance between Tate and Avery was tenuous because at some point she was going to have to tell him the truth. There were times when I questioned Avery's integrity as she allowed the ruse to continue for a protracted period of time, deepening the relationship with not only Tate but his daughter Mandy.<br /><br />The ending was a little anticlimatic but still interesting. When the identity of the killer was revealed, so was another twist. I completely blew it in guessing the real killer but that person was on my short list. <br /><br />This was an interesting book that held my interest throughout, especially listening to it during a long road trip. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11423492509362172650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139656340" />
    <a title="S.M. West" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18424676-s-m-west"><img alt="S.M. West" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564323942p2/18424676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139656340?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.M. West" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.M. West" href="/user/show/18424676-s-m-west">S.M. West</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139656340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1148464128639397188"><b>4.5 SENATOR STARS</b><br/><br/>Well, Ms. Brown is quickly becoming one of my go-to authors...she knows how to write and to weave a <b>really good mystery mixed with a danger, intriguing characters and a little bit of sex to keep those juices flowing!</b> I loved this one and so far, Tate and Avery are my fave MCs of SB's books.<br/><br/>Okay, I had my doubts on how you one person could pull off being another person even with the striking resemblance and while for some of it you have to have an open mind, Ms. Brown did a great</span>
  <span id="freeText1148464128639397188" style="display:none"><b>4.5 SENATOR STARS</b><br><br>Well, Ms. Brown is quickly becoming one of my go-to authors...she knows how to write and to weave a <b>really good mystery mixed with a danger, intriguing characters and a little bit of sex to keep those juices flowing!</b> I loved this one and so far, Tate and Avery are my fave MCs of SB's books.<br><br>Okay, I had my doubts on how you one person could pull off being another person even with the striking resemblance and while for some of it you have to have an open mind, Ms. Brown did a great job!<br><br><a href="http://s1292.photobucket.com/user/swidso/media/Mirror_zps8cb4a59d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420069785i/13164406._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo Mirror_zps8cb4a59d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I can't talk about the plot without giving anything away and you are best to go in blind but, what I will say is that she had me guessing for most of the book. While I figured out the ultimate culprit at around the 80% mark and the motive, I still didn't have all the pieces of the puzzle. <br><br>The chemistry between Tate and Avery was <b>palpable, searing and made the whole situation more believable and easier to digest.</b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/95x4Z0q" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420069785ra/13164407.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I highly recommend this book. <b>If you love a great mystery with a few surprises, really complex and intriguing characters...loved Fancy, Irish and Van...and a superbly written story, you must read this book!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1148464128639397188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1332632457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1332632457" />
    <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf"><img alt="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540171256p2/9185509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1332632457?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf">Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1332632457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2729117038006562277">Ok you are going to have to stay with me here. Hear me out... <br/><br/>This story is about Avery Daniels. Avery is a reporter who is in a plane crash and mistakenly identified as Carole Rutledge, the wife of aspiring senatorial candidate, Tate Rutledge. The real Carole Rutledge was also mistaken for Avery, and died in the plane crash. Hence the confusion. Avery and Carole looked so alike that they were often mistaken for each other normally. But Avery's face was totally smashed up in the crash, so nobody</span>
  <span id="freeText2729117038006562277" style="display:none">Ok you are going to have to stay with me here. Hear me out... <br /><br />This story is about Avery Daniels. Avery is a reporter who is in a plane crash and mistakenly identified as Carole Rutledge, the wife of aspiring senatorial candidate, Tate Rutledge. The real Carole Rutledge was also mistaken for Avery, and died in the plane crash. Hence the confusion. Avery and Carole looked so alike that they were often mistaken for each other normally. But Avery's face was totally smashed up in the crash, so nobody could tell. Unfortunately and terrifyingly she is unable to communicate with the doctors and Tate, and her face is completely transformed by plastic surgery to resemble Carole. <br /><br />Just as Avery is about to reveal the truth to Carole's husband Tate in the hospital after she is well enough to speak, she discovers that there is a plan in action to assassinate him. She quite likes Tate at this point, even though she discovers his marriage to Carole was extremely turbulent . Anyway she doesn't want him to die, and being the reporter that she is, she smells a story in all of this, so she says as Carole to try and figure out who the mastermind behind the assassination plot is. <br /><br />Meanwhile she isn't Carole. And how long can she pretend to be a woman she would have hated, before people start figuring it out??<br /><br />Well..<br /><br />I know I know! You read this synopsis and think "How the hell am I going to enjoy something that is SO UNBELIEVABLE?!". But this is Sandra Brown we are talking about... This is the Queen of romantic suspense! I admit its not exactly "believable" obviously. But if anyone is going to come close, its Sandra Brown! She makes the believability of the story totally irrelevant because its so darn entertaining!! Its like a cool soap opera tale mixed with a good action book! <br /><br />The characters were totally loveable, except for the real Carole, what a piece of work! But Avery was so sweet and Tate was so much more awesome than he could have been. Tate and Carole's daughter Mandy was such a sweetie. His family were fascinating and his tramp-of-a-niece Fancy was a great character too! There really wasn't a character I didn't enjoy reading about.<br /><br />The romance is really sweet. Yes, yes its corny because he doesn't know that she isn't his wife - and how could you NOT KNOW... But damn it - It just works! The sexy scenes are sizzling, the tension is palpable, and the suspense is great! And in typical Sandra Brown style there is an awesome twist at the end that I didn't see coming. It will absolutely be something I will read again, and that is saying something because I don't often waste my reading time re-reading something I have already read!<br /><br />The only criticism I have of this book were of some of the medical scenes. Overall she did a good job, but if you have a breathing tube down your throat connected to the ventilator, you cannot SMELL anything... The tube is bypassing your nose completely. But the medical stuff didn't annoy me enough to change my rating. Which is a lot more than I can say compared to some other books and authors that shall remain nameless.<br /><br />Thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6218.Sandra_Brown" title="Sandra Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Sandra Brown</a>, your books are a constant source of enjoyment for me, thankfully there are so many more for me to get through!!<br /><br /><br />4 Stars because I enjoyed it so damn much!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2729117038006562277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_496190818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/496190818" />
    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/496190818?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/13543626-mirror-image">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=mystery-suspense-with-some-romance">mystery-suspense-with-some-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer496190818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8138592550746569214">Entertaining and enjoyable mystery suspense with some feel good romance at the end.<br/><br/>I questioned some of Avery’s actions, but I’m not sure what I would have done differently.<br/><br/>You need to suspend disbelief that the husband would not sense differences in his wife: her walk, talk, mannerisms, body parts, and scars. Especially since Avery had not studied Carole’s talk and mannerisms. The weakest part was probably the main bad guy. I cannot imagine any person planning, waiting, and doing what he did. B</span>
  <span id="freeText8138592550746569214" style="display:none">Entertaining and enjoyable mystery suspense with some feel good romance at the end.<br /><br />I questioned some of Avery’s actions, but I’m not sure what I would have done differently.<br /><br />You need to suspend disbelief that the husband would not sense differences in his wife: her walk, talk, mannerisms, body parts, and scars. Especially since Avery had not studied Carole’s talk and mannerisms. The weakest part was probably the main bad guy. I cannot imagine any person planning, waiting, and doing what he did. But again if you can suspend disbelief, it makes a good story. It’s good because it’s different and not predictable. It’s not the same kinds of good guys and bad guys that so many other books have.<br /><br />One set of events felt contrived. The hotel operator wouldn’t put through calls to Avery that she wanted to get. And, Irish didn’t tell his assistants that he wanted to take all calls from Avery and Van. And then during a critical time, Irish put himself in places where he couldn’t be reached. If they had cell phones it wouldn’t be a problem. But this book was written before cell phones were common.<br /><br />I don’t know why a killer shot a certain person at the end. I wish the author was clearer about that.<br /><br />Some readers felt the book was too long. I didn’t notice that, probably because I did this as an audiobook. I’m fine with long audiobooks.<br /><br />STORY IDEA FOR OTHER AUTHORS - A STUPID SECONDARY CHARACTER THAT I’D LIKE TO SEE AS A HEROINE:<br />At first, I did not like Francine. But later I was hoping she would uncover something. When that didn’t happen, I realized I’d like to read a story about someone like her. Here she is a minor character. She’s flawed and does stupid things, but her stupidity could be entertaining. Her mother was an alcoholic and never gave enough love and support to Francine. Francine picks up guys in bars and sleeps with almost anyone. She is currently obsessed with Eddie, a cold and remote guy 20 years older. He wants nothing to do with her and insults her. She has no shame and throws herself at him, sneaking into his bedroom and suggestively touching herself and him, wanting sex. One day she bribes a hotel maid to let her in. When he walks in, she says Boo. When he does have sex with her he is rough leaving injuries. She doesn’t seem to mind, probably thinks she deserves it since she was never properly loved by her parents. She searches through Eddie’s things because she is nosy. He can’t get rid of her. He throws her out one day and she’s back and rubbing against him the next. I’d like to see a story where he is keeping secrets, and she finds incriminating evidence about him and doesn’t plan to turn him in but ends up causing him all kinds of trouble, even though she never intends to.<br /><br />In this book, Avery is understanding and kind to Francine which surprises and unsettles Francine. No one has ever treated her that way, but she hesitantly goes along with things Avery suggests. Then she messes up, but then she makes good. One scene made me laugh. While everyone is in a hotel waiting for the next event. Francine is coloring with her 3-year-old-cousin. It surprised me, yet it fit. Here’s this slutty 20-year-old with the emotional maturity of a toddler, doing something a toddler would do - coloring. I don’t remember Francine’s exact age - something over 18.<br /><br />NARRATOR:<br />The narrator Dick Hill was good in this book. Very different from his reading Slow Heat in Heaven. I did not like his interpretations in that book.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: 3rd person. Unabridged audiobook length: 14 hrs and 51 mins. Swearing language: strong, including religious swear words, but rarely used. Sexual language: moderate, but not often used. Number of sex scenes: about 9, short with not much detail. Setting: 1990 Texas. Book copyright: 1990. Genre: mystery suspense with some romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8138592550746569214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martel" href="/user/show/40865087-martel">Martel</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9673444514337629254">Far fetched and sometimes bordering on ludicrous, this novel still remains quite entertaining. The greatest shortcoming of the book is (in my eyes) the hero's job.<br/>A politician !<br/>Of all the possible professions, this is one of the worst for a character that isn't the villain. <br/>I get that this is some kind of cultural clash, and that politicians are not perceived in every countries as dishonest, manipulative, hypocritical and power-hungry turncoats, but still this one was hard to swallow. <br/>That the w</span>
  <span id="freeText9673444514337629254" style="display:none">Far fetched and sometimes bordering on ludicrous, this novel still remains quite entertaining. The greatest shortcoming of the book is (in my eyes) the hero's job.<br />A politician !<br />Of all the possible professions, this is one of the worst for a character that isn't the villain. <br />I get that this is some kind of cultural clash, and that politicians are not perceived in every countries as dishonest, manipulative, hypocritical and power-hungry turncoats, but still this one was hard to swallow. <br />That the whole plot was based on one huge lie from the heroine, pretending to be someone else and especially deceiving a child, impersonating her deceased mother, this was a bit hard on me too. <br />So I don't really know if it was just me or the book, but as absorbing as the novel was, I couldn't rate it higher.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2673767756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2673767756" />
    <a title="Georgie-who-is-Sarah-Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9572229-georgie-who-is-sarah-drew"><img alt="Georgie-who-is-Sarah-Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408401009p2/9572229.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2673767756?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Georgie-who-is-Sarah-Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Georgie-who-is-Sarah-Drew" href="/user/show/9572229-georgie-who-is-sarah-drew">Georgie-who-is-Sarah-Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17449594-mirror-image">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9572229-georgie-who-is-sarah-drew?shelf=archived">archived</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9572229-georgie-who-is-sarah-drew?shelf=tag-reviewed">tag-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9572229-georgie-who-is-sarah-drew?shelf=genre-tec">genre-tec</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2673767756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12475708374835339040">This is the first line of "Mirror Image" - <br/>"The hell of it was that it couldn't have been a better day for flying." <br/>And, straightaway, you know there's going to be a plane crash.<br/><br/>The hell of it is that it couldn't have been a better first line. So much potential, the first quarter of the book. The excitement as the story gets off the ground, the tension ratcheting up as the h lies helpless to save herself in a hospital bed, the drama of an unseen assassin whispering threats in the night. <br/><br/>And then</span>
  <span id="freeText12475708374835339040" style="display:none">This is the first line of "Mirror Image" - <br />"The hell of it was that it couldn't have been a better day for flying." <br />And, straightaway, you know there's going to be a plane crash.<br /><br />The hell of it is that it couldn't have been a better first line. So much potential, the first quarter of the book. The excitement as the story gets off the ground, the tension ratcheting up as the h lies helpless to save herself in a hospital bed, the drama of an unseen assassin whispering threats in the night. <br /><br />And then - well, then there's a book crash. Our plucky h becomes abruptly TSTL and makes some logically and ethically indefensible decisions. Not the least of which is to launch herself into love with a man she knows to despise her, and whose only apparent virtue is to send her daily flowers for PR purposes. <br /><br />This was a buddy-read with Lyuda, Linda, Luli, Nadine &amp; Nefise (my first BR - thanks for the ride, fellas!) and - honestly - if it hadn't been, I don't think I would have bothered with the rest of the story, which was both dated and illogical. I also really struggled with all the relationships shown in the book - with the exception of the plot-moppet, there wasn't one that wasn't toxic to some degree. <br /><br />The book was written in 1990, and it really does show; I realise that our awareness of respectful language and gender relations has come on a long way since then, so I'll give Sandra Brown a partial pass on things. But it doesn't mean I like them. For instance, the H (a very generic bland H) casually refers to an off-stage woman he disapproves of as, "That dyke." There are some throw-back comments on gender that didn't do much for me either -<br />"She wanted to defend herself against his criticism, to fight back with a woman's weapons. [<i>Eh? what are they?</i>] Because, while his fierce temperament was intimidating, it was also arousing."<br />and<br />"Her body received him coyly because he was very large and hard and she was very small and soft. Man and woman. As it should be."<br /><br />But I could live (just) with the style if the plot itself made sense. Tell you a secret? It doesn't. Consolingly, my BR pals were just as flustered by the h's choices, the villain's motivations, the inconsistent actions of several key minor characters. I also need to <i>respect</i> my MCs; even if they don't behave as I would, I need to be given <u>credible</u> motives for their actions. Didn't happen.<br /><br />To be fair to "Mirror Image", there were good things - the tension at the start was really impressive: SB did a great job of conveying the h's frantic state of mind. Also, reading back through the villain's scenes, some of their utterances (which seemed pretty banal at the time) took on an intriguing new resonance. And my favourite character made it through sorta intact. <br /><br />Honestly, though? A plane crash.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12475708374835339040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2333259211697982120">This is one of the most amazing books I have read in a very long time. Avery Daniels is a has-been television reporter on her way to cover a story in Dallas when her plan crashes almost immediately after take-off. <br/>Also on the plane are Carole Rutledge and her 3 yr old daughter Mandy. Carole's husband, Tate, is running for the senate seat in Texas.<br/>Avery manages to evacuate the burning plane with Mandy in tow and is mistakenly identified as Carole Rutledge. Unable to immediately communicate and te</span>
  <span id="freeText2333259211697982120" style="display:none">This is one of the most amazing books I have read in a very long time. Avery Daniels is a has-been television reporter on her way to cover a story in Dallas when her plan crashes almost immediately after take-off. <br />Also on the plane are Carole Rutledge and her 3 yr old daughter Mandy. Carole's husband, Tate, is running for the senate seat in Texas.<br />Avery manages to evacuate the burning plane with Mandy in tow and is mistakenly identified as Carole Rutledge. Unable to immediately communicate and tell everyone she's not who they think she is Avery is forced to take on the roll of Carole Rutledge in order to save her own life, the life of Tate Rutledge and help Mandy recover from the horrifying plane crash. <br />This book has it all: action, romance, suspense and mystery, aggravation at certain characters' behavior, sympathy...you name it.<br />And to beat it all, I had no clue who was behind the threats made against Tate; I never saw "that" coming nor the reasons behind the character's actions.<br />This is definitely a book I will probably check out again!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10056992252684837200">3.95 enjoyable stars. <br/><br/>I really liked this one. It is my first Sandra Brown book and probably won't be my last. I was so engaged I stayed up til 4:30am to finish it. <br/><br/>I found it so far fateched but it was still super engaging. My biggest complaint with the story is that the "HEA" was the cruelest of morsels the author fed the reader.   <span id="freeText10056992252684837200" style="display:none">3.95 enjoyable stars. <br /><br />I really liked this one. It is my first Sandra Brown book and probably won't be my last. I was so engaged I stayed up til 4:30am to finish it. <br /><br />I found it so far fateched but it was still super engaging. My biggest complaint with the story is that the "HEA" was the cruelest of morsels the author fed the reader. It was a pretty long book and I waited and waited and waited some more for the MCs to vocalize their love for each other and get on the same page... the epilogue was pretty much crap. We got a single sweet BAM and that was it. We never got to enjoy their love for each other or his sweet "untainted by hate" side. Other than the ending which I was highly dissapointed in I sincerely enjoyed this "who dun it", "will they/won't they?" love story. <br /><br />I'd give a kidney for there to be a book two! </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9POD0RlKc0FeiN3xveQcJyJRs644KOdDe+KsDjPO00ngyGoUVUEQvK4cSa/TKRzzFZigLHEDIcc26r/jMq/knw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6zJLnKulL7zyTXph/qM8l/RvROlcXcYD5Klv6um/m0z/CaJZ565MQQLZ7j+QbjxDw6ZXaxV2AIepoXwH6N6smg==')})
  }

El patriarca de los Agramunt, Biel, decide encontrar a su nieto y un mes después, cuando Lucas regresa a su casa en la Barceloneta le espera un lujoso automóvil aparcado frente a su puerta.\nA partir de ese momento, la vida de Lucas dará un giro radical: deberá abandonar la única vida que ha conocido, será educado con disciplina y se enfrentará a los otros aspirantes a la herencia de su abuelo.\nEncerrado entre los muros de una suntuosa mansión y mientras intenta adaptarse a ese mundo desconocido que lo rechaza, conocerá a Alicia, la joven que le ayudará y le enseñará lo que es el amor y hasta qué punto estar atrapado puede ser la salvación de un hombre.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11472005520434872261\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return <span id="freeTextContainer6862421819450582312"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a> </i> <br/><br/>Sandra Brown is the author of more than sixty New York Times bestsellers, including STING (2016), FRICTION (2015), MEAN STREAK (2014), DEADLINE(2013), & LOW PRESSURE (2012), LETHAL (2011).<br/><br/>Brown began her writing career in 1981 and since then has published over seventy nove</span>
  <span id="freeText6862421819450582312" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a> </i> <br /><br />Sandra Brown is the author of more than sixty New York Times bestsellers, including STING (2016), FRICTION (2015), MEAN STREAK (2014), DEADLINE(2013), &amp; LOW PRESSURE (2012), LETHAL (2011).<br /><br />Brown began her writing career in 1981 and since then has published over seventy novels, bringing the number of copies of her books in print worldwide to upwards of eighty million. Her work has been translated into over thirty languages.<br /><br />In 2009 Brown detoured from romantic suspense to write, Rainwater, a much acclaimed, powerfully moving historical fiction story about honor and sacrifice during the Great Depression.<br /> <br />Brown was given an honorary Doctorate of Humane Letters from Texas Christian University. She was named Thriller Master for 2008, the top award given by the International Thriller Writer’s Association. Other awards and commendations include the 2007 Texas Medal of Arts Award for Literature and the Romance Writers of America’s Lifetime Achievement Award. <br /></span>
